<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Non-Aligned Movement</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="line-height:11pt"><b>Website</b><br/>

</td>

<p>The <b>Non-Aligned Movement</b> (<b>NAM</b>) is a group of states that are not formally aligned with or against any major <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Power_bloc" title="Power bloc">power bloc</a>. As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the movement has 120 members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-members_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-members-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>The organization was founded in <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> in 1961, and was largely conceived by India's first prime minister, <a href="/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru" title="Jawaharlal Nehru">Jawaharlal Nehru</a>; Indonesia's first president, <a href="/wiki/Sukarno" title="Sukarno">Sukarno</a>; Egypt's second president, <a href="/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser" title="Gamal Abdel Nasser">Gamal Abdel Nasser</a>; Ghana's first president <a href="/wiki/Kwame_Nkrumah" title="Kwame Nkrumah">Kwame Nkrumah</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia's</a> president, <a href="/wiki/Josip_Broz_Tito" title="Josip Broz Tito">Josip Broz Tito</a>. All five leaders were prominent advocates of a middle course for states in the <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">Developing World</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Western_Bloc" title="Western Bloc">Western</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Blocs</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>. The phrase itself was first used to represent the doctrine by Indian diplomat <a href="/wiki/V._K._Krishna_Menon" title="V. K. Krishna Menon">V. K. Krishna Menon</a> in 1953, at the United Nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a speech given during the <i>Havana Declaration of 1979</i>, <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a> said the purpose of the organization is to ensure "the national independence, sovereignty, territorial integrity and security of non-aligned countries" in their "struggle against <a href="/wiki/Imperialism" title="Imperialism">imperialism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonialism</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neo-colonialism" title="Neo-colonialism">neo-colonialism</a>, racism, and all forms of foreign aggression, <a href="/wiki/Military_occupation" title="Military occupation">occupation</a>, domination, interference or <a href="/wiki/Hegemony" title="Hegemony">hegemony</a> as well as against <a href="/wiki/Great_power" title="Great power">great power</a> and bloc politics".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> The countries of the Non-Aligned Movement represent nearly two-thirds of the United Nations's members and contain 55% of the world population. Membership is particularly concentrated in countries considered to be <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing</a> or part of the <a href="/wiki/Third_World" title="Third World">Third World</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>Members have at times included the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a>, Argentina, Zaire, Cyprus, and Malta. Although many of the Non-Aligned Movement's members were actually quite closely aligned with one or another of the <a href="/wiki/Superpower" title="Superpower">superpowers</a>, the movement still maintained cohesion throughout the Cold War. Some members were involved in serious conflicts with other members (e.g. India and Pakistan, Iran and Iraq). The movement fractured from its own internal contradictions when the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_war_in_Afghanistan" title="Soviet war in Afghanistan">Soviet Union invaded Afghanistan</a> in 1979. Although the Soviet allies supported the invasion, other members of the movement (particularly <a href="/wiki/Muslim_world" title="Muslim world">predominantly Muslim states</a>) condemned it.</p>
<p>Because the Non-Aligned Movement was formed as an attempt to thwart the Cold War,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-suvedi_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-suvedi-6">[6]</a></sup> it has struggled to find relevance since the Cold War ended. After the <a href="/wiki/Breakup_of_Yugoslavia" title="Breakup of Yugoslavia">breakup of Yugoslavia</a>, a founding member, its membership was <a href="/wiki/Suspension_(punishment)" title="Suspension (punishment)">suspended</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-suspended_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-suspended-7">[7]</a></sup> in 1992 at the regular Ministerial Meeting of the Movement, held in New York during the regular yearly session of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">General Assembly of the United Nations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Najam_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Najam-9">[9]</a></sup> The successor states of the Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia have expressed little interest in membership, though <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> have observer status. In 2004, Malta and Cyprus ceased to be members and joined the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a> is the only member of the Movement in Europe. <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> and Fiji are the most recent entrants, joining in 2011. The applications of Bosnia and Herzegovina and Costa Rica were rejected in 1995 and 1998, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Najam_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-Najam-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/16th_Summit_of_the_Non-Aligned_Movement" title="16th Summit of the Non-Aligned Movement">16th NAM summit</a> took place in <a href="/wiki/Tehran" title="Tehran">Tehran</a>, Iran, from 26 to 31 August 2012. According to <a href="/wiki/Mehr_News_Agency" title="Mehr News Agency">Mehr News Agency</a>, representatives from over 150 countries were scheduled to attend.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MehrNews_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-MehrNews-10">[10]</a></sup> Attendance at the highest level includes 27 presidents, 2 kings and emirs, 7 prime ministers, 9 vice presidents, 2 parliament spokesmen and 5 special envoys.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tehrantimes1_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-tehrantimes1-11">[11]</a></sup> At the summit, Iran took over from Egypt as Chair of the Non-Aligned Movement for the period 2012 to 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allafrica_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-allafrica-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Non-Aligned movement was never established as a formal organization, but became the name to refer to the participants of the <i>Conference of Heads of State or Government of Non-Aligned Countries</i> first held in 1961. The term "non-alignment" was established in 1953 at the United Nations. Nehru used the phrase in a 1954 speech in Colombo, Sri Lanka. In this speech, Nehru described the five pillars to be used as a guide for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sino-Indian_relations" title="Sino-Indian relations">Sino-Indian relations</a> called <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Panchsheel" title="Panchsheel">Panchsheel</a></i> (five restraints), these principles would later serve as the basis of the Non-Aligned Movement. The five principles were:</p>
<ul>
<li>Mutual respect for each other's territorial integrity and <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a></li>
<li>Mutual non-aggression</li>
<li>Mutual non-interference in domestic affairs</li>
<li>Equality and mutual benefit</li>
<li>Peaceful co-existence</li>
</ul>
<p>A significant milestone in the development of the Non-Aligned Movement was the 1955 <a href="/wiki/Bandung_Conference" title="Bandung Conference">Bandung Conference</a>, a conference of Asian and African states hosted by Indonesian president <a href="/wiki/Sukarno" title="Sukarno">Sukarno</a>, who gave a significant contribution to promote this movement. Bringing together Sukarno, U Nu, Nasser, Nehru, Tito, Nkrumah and Menon with the likes of <a href="/wiki/Ho_Chi_Minh" title="Ho Chi Minh">Ho Chi Minh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zhou_Enlai" title="Zhou Enlai">Zhou Enlai</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Norodom_Sihanouk" title="Norodom Sihanouk">Norodom Sihanouk</a>, as well as U Thant and a young <a href="/wiki/Indira_Gandhi" title="Indira Gandhi">Indira Gandhi</a>, the conference adopted a "declaration on promotion of world peace and cooperation", which included Nehru's five principles, and a collective pledge to remain neutral in the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>. Six years after Bandung, an initiative of Yugoslav president <a href="/wiki/Josip_Broz_Tito" title="Josip Broz Tito">Josip Broz Tito</a> led to the first <i>Conference of Heads of State or Government of Non-Aligned Countries</i>, which was held in September 1961 in <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The term <i>non-aligned movement</i> appears first in the fifth conference in 1976, where participating countries are denoted as <i>members of the movement</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Belgrade_Conference,_1961.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2483" data-file-width="3336" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Belgrade_Conference%2C_1961.jpg/220px-Belgrade_Conference%2C_1961.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Belgrade_Conference%2C_1961.jpg/330px-Belgrade_Conference%2C_1961.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Belgrade_Conference%2C_1961.jpg/440px-Belgrade_Conference%2C_1961.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Belgrade_Conference,_1961.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Belgrade Conference, September 1961.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the Lusaka Conference in September 1970, the member nations added as aims of the movement the peaceful resolution of disputes and the abstention from the big power military alliances and pacts. Another added aim was opposition to stationing of military bases in foreign countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-suvedi_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-suvedi-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>The founding fathers of the Non-Aligned Movement were: <a href="/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru" title="Jawaharlal Nehru">Jawaharlal Nehru</a> of India, <a href="/wiki/Sukarno" title="Sukarno">Sukarno</a> of Indonesia, <a href="/wiki/Josip_Broz_Tito" title="Josip Broz Tito">Josip Broz Tito</a> of <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gamal_Abdul_Nasser" title="Gamal Abdul Nasser">Gamal Abdul Nasser</a> of Egypt and <a href="/wiki/Kwame_Nkrumah" title="Kwame Nkrumah">Kwame Nkrumah</a> of Ghana. Their actions were known as 'The Initiative of Five'.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organizational_structure_and_membership">Organizational structure and membership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Organizational structure and membership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The movement stems from a desire not to be aligned within a geopolitical/military structure and therefore itself does not have a very strict organizational structure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-organizational_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-organizational-2">[2]</a></sup> Some organizational basics were defined at the 1996 <i>Cartagena Document on Methodology</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Methodology_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Methodology-15">[15]</a></sup> The Summit Conference of Heads of State or Government of Non-Aligned States is "the highest decision making authority". The chairmanship rotates between countries and changes at every summit of heads of state or government to the country organizing the summit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Methodology_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-Methodology-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Requirements for membership of the Non-Aligned Movement coincide with the key beliefs of the United Nations. The current requirements are that the candidate country has displayed practices in accordance with the ten "Bandung principles" of 1955:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Methodology_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-Methodology-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Respect for fundamental human rights and for the purposes and principles of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charter_of_the_United_Nations" title="Charter of the United Nations">Charter of the United Nations</a>.</li>
<li>Respect for the sovereignty and territorial integrity of all nations.</li>
<li>Recognition of the movements for national independence.</li>
<li>Recognition of the equality of all races and of the equality of all nations, large and small.</li>
<li>Abstention from intervention or interference in the internal affairs of another country.</li>
<li>Respect for the right of each nation to defend itself singly or collectively, in conformity with the Charter of the United Nations.</li>
<li>Refraining from acts or threats of aggression or the use of force against the territorial integrity or political independence of any country.</li>
<li>Settlement of all international disputes by peaceful means, in conformity with the Charter of the United Nations.</li>
<li>Promotion of mutual interests and co-operation.</li>
<li>Respect for justice and international obligations.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Policies_and_ideology">Policies and ideology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Policies and ideology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Non-Aligned_Movement_(emblem_-_South_Africa_Conference).png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="255" data-file-width="279" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/20/Non-Aligned_Movement_%28emblem_-_South_Africa_Conference%29.png/220px-Non-Aligned_Movement_%28emblem_-_South_Africa_Conference%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/2/20/Non-Aligned_Movement_%28emblem_-_South_Africa_Conference%29.png 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Non-Aligned_Movement_(emblem_-_South_Africa_Conference).png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The South Africa Conference NAM logo.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Secretaries General of the NAM had included such diverse figures as <a href="/wiki/Suharto" title="Suharto">Suharto</a>, a corrupt<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> and militaristic<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> anti-communist, and <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela" title="Nelson Mandela">Nelson Mandela</a>, a democratic socialist and famous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internal_resistance_to_South_African_apartheid" title="Internal resistance to South African apartheid">anti-apartheid</a> activist. Consisting of many governments with vastly different ideologies, the Non-Aligned Movement is unified by its declared commitment to <a href="/wiki/World_peace" title="World peace">world peace</a> and security. At the seventh summit held in New Delhi in March 1983, the movement described itself as "history's biggest peace movement".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thomas_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-thomas-19">[19]</a></sup> The movement places equal emphasis on <a href="/wiki/Disarmament" title="Disarmament">disarmament</a>. NAM's commitment to peace pre-dates its formal <a href="/wiki/Institutionalisation" title="Institutionalisation">institutionalisation</a> in 1961. The Brioni meeting between heads of governments of India, Egypt and Yugoslavia in 1956 recognized that there exists a vital link between struggle for peace and endeavours for <a href="/wiki/Disarmament" title="Disarmament">disarmament</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thomas_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-thomas-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 1970s and early 1980s, the NAM also sponsored campaigns for restructuring commercial relations between developed and developing nations, namely the <a href="/wiki/New_International_Economic_Order" title="New International Economic Order">New International Economic Order</a> (NIEO), and its cultural offspring, the <a href="/wiki/New_World_Information_and_Communication_Order" title="New World Information and Communication Order">New World Information and Communication Order</a> (NWICO). The latter, on its own, sparked a Non-Aligned initiative on cooperation for communications, the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_News_Agencies_Pool" title="Non-Aligned News Agencies Pool">Non-Aligned News Agencies Pool</a>, created in 1975 and later converted into the <a href="/wiki/NAM_News_Network" title="NAM News Network">NAM News Network</a> in 2005.</p>
<p>The Non-Aligned Movement espouses policies and practices of cooperation, especially those that are multilateral and provide mutual benefit to all those involved. Many of the members of the Non-Aligned Movement are also members of the United Nations. Both organisations have a stated policy of peaceful cooperation, yet the successes the NAM has had with multilateral agreements tend to be ignored by the larger, western and developed nation dominated UN.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-20">[20]</a></sup> African concerns about apartheid were linked with Arab-Asian concerns about Palestine<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-20">[20]</a></sup> and multilateral cooperation in these areas has enjoyed moderate success. The Non-Aligned Movement has played a major role in various <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ideological" title="Ideological">ideological</a> conflicts throughout its existence, including extreme opposition to apartheid governments and support of guerrilla movements in various locations, including <a href="/wiki/Rhodesia" title="Rhodesia">Rhodesia</a> and South Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Role_after_the_Cold_War">Role after the Cold War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Role after the Cold War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Since the end of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, the Non-Aligned Movement has been forced to redefine itself and reinvent its purpose in the current world system. A major question has been whether many of its foundational ideologies, principally national independence, territorial integrity, and the struggle against colonialism and imperialism, can be applied to contemporary issues. The movement has emphasised its principles of multilateralism, equality, and mutual non-aggression in attempting to become a stronger voice for the global South, and an instrument that can be utilised to promote the needs of member nations at the international level and strengthen their political leverage when negotiating with developed nations. In its efforts to advance Southern interests, the movement has stressed the importance of cooperation and unity amongst member states,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-21">[21]</a></sup> but as in the past, cohesion remains a problem since the size of the organisation and the divergence of agendas and allegiances present the ongoing potential for fragmentation. While agreement on basic principles has been smooth, taking definitive action vis-à-vis particular international issues has been rare, with the movement preferring to assert its criticism or support rather than pass hard-line resolutions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>The movement continues to see a role for itself, as in its view, the world's poorest nations remain exploited and marginalised, no longer by opposing superpowers, but rather in a uni-polar world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> and it is Western hegemony and neo-colonialism that the movement has really re-aligned itself against. It opposes foreign occupation, interference in internal affairs and aggressive unilateral measures, but it has also shifted to focus on the socio-economic challenges facing member states, especially the inequalities manifested by globalization and the implications of neo-liberal policies. The Non-Aligned Movement has identified economic <a href="/wiki/Underdevelopment" title="Underdevelopment">underdevelopment</a>, poverty, and social injustices as growing threats to peace and security.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_activities_and_positions">Current activities and positions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Current activities and positions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl>
<dt>Criticism of US policy</dt>
</dl>
<p>In recent years the organization has criticized certain aspects of US foreign policy. The <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">2003 invasion of Iraq</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_on_Terrorism" title="War on Terrorism">War on Terrorism</a>, its attempts to stifle <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>'s nuclear plans, and its other actions have been denounced by some members of the Non-Aligned Movement as attempts to run roughshod over the sovereignty of smaller nations; at the most recent summit, <a href="/wiki/Kim_Yong-nam" title="Kim Yong-nam">Kim Yong-nam</a>, the head of North Korea's parliament, stated that, "The United States is attempting to deprive other countries of even their legitimate right to peaceful nuclear activities."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Self-determination of Puerto Rico</dt>
</dl>
<p>Since 1961, the organization has supported the discussion of the case of <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Political status of Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico's self-determination</a> before the United Nations. A resolution on the matter was to be proposed on the XV Summit by the <a href="/wiki/Hostosian_National_Independence_Movement" title="Hostosian National Independence Movement">Hostosian National Independence Movement</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Precise_language" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The text near this tag is dated.">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Self-determination of Western Sahara</dt>
</dl>
<p>Since 1973, the group has supported the discussion of the case of <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara_conflict" title="Western Sahara conflict">Western Sahara's self-determination</a> before the United Nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The movement reaffirmed in its last meeting (Sharm El Sheikh 2009) the support to the Self-determination of the <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_people" title="Sahrawi people">Sahrawi</a> people by choosing between any valid option, welcomed the direct conversations between the parties, and remembered the responsibility of the United Nations on the Sahrawi issue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Sustainable development</dt>
</dl>
<p>The movement is publicly committed to the tenets of <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_development" title="Sustainable development">sustainable development</a> and the attainment of the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goals" title="Millennium Development Goals">Millennium Development Goals</a>, but it believes that the international community has not created conditions conducive to development and has infringed upon the right to sovereign development by each member state. Issues such as globalization, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_countries%27_debt" title="Developing countries' debt">debt burden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trade_justice" title="Trade justice">unfair trade practices</a>, the decline in foreign aid, <a href="/wiki/Conditionality" title="Conditionality">donor conditionality</a>, and the lack of democracy in international financial decision-making are cited as factors inhibiting development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Reforms of the UN</dt>
</dl>
<p>The movement has been outspoken in its criticism of current UN structures and power dynamics, stating that the organisation has been utilised by powerful states in ways that violate the movement's principles. It has made a number of recommendations that it says would strengthen the representation and power of "non-aligned" states. The proposed <a href="/wiki/Reform_of_the_United_Nations" title="Reform of the United Nations">UN reforms</a> are also aimed at improving the transparency and democracy of UN decision-making. The UN Security Council is the element it considers the most distorted, undemocratic, and in need of reshaping.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South-South_cooperation" title="South-South cooperation">South-South cooperation</a></dt>
</dl>
<p>The movement has collaborated with other organisations of the developing world –  primarily the <a href="/wiki/Group_of_77" title="Group of 77">Group of 77</a> –  forming a number of joint committees and releasing statements and documents representing the shared interests of both groups. This dialogue and cooperation can be taken as an effort to increase the global awareness about the organisation and bolster its political clout.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Cultural diversity and human rights</dt>
</dl>
<p>The movement accepts the universality of human rights and social justice, but fiercely resists cultural homogenisation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="reliable source needed for the whole sentence (August 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In line with its views on sovereignty, the organisation appeals for the protection of cultural diversity, and the tolerance of the religious, socio-cultural, and historical particularities that define human rights in a specific region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (August 2012)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Working groups, task forces, committees<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></dt>
</dl>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ul>
<li>Committee on Palestine</li>
<li>High-Level Working Group for the Restructuring of the United Nations</li>
<li>Joint Coordinating Committee (chaired by Chairman of G-77 and Chairman of NAM)</li>
<li>Non-Aligned Security Caucus</li>
<li>Standing Ministerial Committee for Economic Cooperation</li>
<li>Task Force on Somalia</li>
<li>Working Group on Disarmament</li>
<li>Working Group on Human Rights</li>
<li>Working Group on Peace-Keeping Operations</li>
</ul>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Summits">Summits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Summits">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Meeting_of_the_heads_of_state_at_the_16th_summit_of_the_NAM_(1).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="583" data-file-width="900" height="259" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Meeting_of_the_heads_of_state_at_the_16th_summit_of_the_NAM_%281%29.jpg/400px-Meeting_of_the_heads_of_state_at_the_16th_summit_of_the_NAM_%281%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Meeting_of_the_heads_of_state_at_the_16th_summit_of_the_NAM_%281%29.jpg/600px-Meeting_of_the_heads_of_state_at_the_16th_summit_of_the_NAM_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Meeting_of_the_heads_of_state_at_the_16th_summit_of_the_NAM_%281%29.jpg/800px-Meeting_of_the_heads_of_state_at_the_16th_summit_of_the_NAM_%281%29.jpg 2x" width="400"/></a>

16th summit of the NAM, Tehran</div>
</div>
</div>

<p>A variety of ministerial meetings are held between the summit meetings. Some are specialist, such as the meeting on "Inter-Faith Dialogue and Co-operation for Peace", held in Manila, the Philippines, 16–18 March 2010. There is a general Conference of Foreign Ministers every three years. The most recent were in Bali, Indonesia, 23–27 May 2011 and Algiers, Algeria, 26–29 May 2014.</p>
<p>The Non-Aligned Movement celebrated its 50th anniversary in Belgrade on 5–6 September 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Secretary_Generals">Secretary Generals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Secretary Generals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(April 2011)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Between summits, the Non-Aligned Movement is run by the Secretary General elected at the last summit meeting. The Coordinating Bureau, also based at the UN, is the main instrument for directing the work of the movement's task forces, committees and working groups.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Members.2C_observers_and_guests">Members, observers and guests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Members, observers and guests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_members">Current members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Current members">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following countries are members of the NAM, arranged by continent, showing their year of admission:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-members_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-members-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Currently every African country (except the newly created <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a>) is a member of the Non-Aligned Movement.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Observers">Observers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Observers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Guests">Guests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Guests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There is no permanent guest status,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> but often several non-member countries are represented as guests at conferences. In addition, a large number of organisations, both from within the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_system" title="UN system">UN system</a> and from outside, are always invited as guests.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Presidency">Presidency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Presidency">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>NAM's presidency changes every three years. Venezuela currently holds the Presidency of the Non-Aligned Movement,which was hosted to Nicolas Madura and hosted the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=17th_Summit_of_the_Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="17th Summit of the Non-Aligned Movement (page does not exist)">17th NAM summit</a>,</p>

<li id="cite_note-38"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-38">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In a joint letter to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_Secretary-General" title="UN Secretary-General">UN Secretary-General</a> sent just prior to unification, the Ministers of Foreign affairs of North and South Yemen stated that "All treaties and agreements concluded between either the Yemen Arab Republic or the People's Democratic Republic of Yemen and other States and international organizations in accordance with international law which are in force on 22 May 1990 will remain in effect, and international relations existing on 22 May 1990 between the People's Democratic Republic of Yemen and the Yemen Arab Republic and other States will continue."<cite class="citation book">Bühler, Konrad (2001). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=Ty7NAG1Jl-8C&amp;dq=State+Succession+and+Membership+in+International+Organizations&amp;source=gbs_navlinks_s" rel="nofollow"><i>State Succession and Membership in International Organizations</i></a>. Martinus Nijhoff Publisher.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANon-Aligned+Movement&amp;rft.aufirst=Konrad&amp;rft.aulast=B%C3%BChler&amp;rft.btitle=State+Succession+and+Membership+in+International+Organizations&amp;rft.date=2001&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DTy7NAG1Jl-8C%26dq%3DState%2BSuccession%2Band%2BMembership%2Bin%2BInternational%2BOrganizations%26source%3Dgbs_navlinks_s&amp;rft.pub=Martinus+Nijhoff+Publisher&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-39"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-39">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Flag_of_North_Yemen.svg/23px-Flag_of_North_Yemen.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Flag_of_North_Yemen.svg/35px-Flag_of_North_Yemen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Flag_of_North_Yemen.svg/45px-Flag_of_North_Yemen.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Yemen_Arab_Republic" title="Yemen Arab Republic">North Yemen</a> is one of the founders in 1961. <span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1800" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Flag_of_South_Yemen.svg/23px-Flag_of_South_Yemen.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Flag_of_South_Yemen.svg/35px-Flag_of_South_Yemen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Flag_of_South_Yemen.svg/45px-Flag_of_South_Yemen.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Democratic_Republic_of_Yemen" title="People's Democratic Republic of Yemen">South Yemen</a> joined in 1970. In 1990 both were <a href="/wiki/Yemeni_unification" title="Yemeni unification">unified</a> into a single state which accepted responsibility for all treaties of its predecessors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></span></li>
